<review>I really wanted to like this place because it is a lot cheaper than the place I usually go to, but the service was simply sub-par. I went in today for acrylic nails and gel polish on my fingernails. The woman who did my nails (the oldest lady there, so I assumed most experienced) was unfriendly and gruff, even though I told her it was my first time there and was interested in finding a new salon. She was very rough with my hands! She cut me twice with her electric file and she literally gave my hand a little slap each time she wanted me to switch which hand was under the light. She did not have the color I had chosen from their options, but we found an other which was fine. The most irritating thing is that she refused to give me a rounded-square tip. She kept showing me on a nail remnant what my options were: SUPER square (almost duck-bill shape) or SUPER round. < review>
I was very disappointed with this salon. I was in town for work and needing to kill a couple hours while waiting for my flight out of town. I planned to see my normal salon when I was back in town but I was in the Redlands area and searched for a salon with good reviews. The salon itself was run down, dirty, and hot inside. I got a pedicure and a gel manicure. In neither did the nail tech clean underneath my nails. During the pedicure he didn't take care of the sides of my big toe nails, where ingrowns can easily start if they aren't maintained. He didn't even buff the nails at all and they had dis colored slightly from having dark polish on. The massages for both were a matter of seconds in length and completely wimpy in pressure/technique. I should have waited until I got home.<//review>

<Review>Pricey.. but man.. what a meal (the BBQ at your table feast).  The meats were pre-seasoned.. but you cook them at the table with various add on seasonsings like soy bean paste (yum! never had that before), raw garlic, kimchees, etc.  What an incredible set of flavors. I've had a bit of korean BBQ.. even made my own at home. but I was so glad t otry these guys out and see how it's really done. Was a bit expensive.. and I would have appreciated a bit of coaching on what flavors go with what. espcecially for folks who have never had Korean and get a table full of raw + picked ingredients, and a pair of sissors.. hehe.. they muc hreally be confused. But I was a happy camper there tonight. Just dom't "over kimchee" as I often do, or your spouse/friends may complain for the next couple of days.. ;)<//Review>< pictures>

<review>So happy I found another great Korean place near my new place. Korean BBQ House is a full-on Korean restaurant complete with grill at your table BBQs, all you can eat BBQ specials, and a variety of non-bbq dishes.

They seem super authentic, because there are a bunch of dishes that I've never seen before. Everybody knows that's the marker of an authentic ethnic restaurant, right?

The $20 AYCE BBQ special lets you choose between two options (see one of the photos). Sounds pretty cool.

They give you a variety of banchan - 8 when I ate there, but from other Yelpers pictures, more if you do bbq. Both the tofu soup and kimchi pancake were spot on. The tofu soup came piping hot - almost scalding my tongue, lots of beef, rich broth, and big portion of tofu.

Service was quick and courteous. Definitely worth a go!< /review><Gmap_id>0x808f79883aefecb5:0x90af3e40e4053b2a</Gmap_id><pictures>None<//pictures><rating>4< /rating><resp>None<//resp><user>101220706149966390072< /user></record>

<rate>5<//rate><review>Discovering this restaurant early last year was one of the best parts of my 2020! This restaurant is wonderful! The prices are very reasonable, the portions are great, and the quality is delicious!! We've gone multiple times before the pandemic, as well as done takeout now that indoor dining is closed, and have never been disappointed. We have eaten here with multiple family friends, and no one has had anything but good things to say about their orders. Their pasta dishes are a favorite of mine, particularly the linguine alfredo and penne filletto, and my friends raved for days about their lamb entree. Delicious dessert here as well - I always get the tiramisu.
Indoor dining experience (pre- Covid-19): We love dining in here! It's a smaller, more intimate restaurant setting, and there seem to often be regulars around. Our server Elena is always very patient, even with larger groups or first timers who don't know what to order, and very helpful with recommendations (including the wine!). You can look into a portion of the kitchen and enjoy watching your meal prepared. Such a wonderful and homey feel to this place!

Smallish location compared to others, with a lot of equipment neatly packed in. What stood out was the service, which was friendly and not too intimidating. It‚Äôs been a while since I‚Äôve been in a gym for a formal workout and expected some meathead to look down on my lack of physicality :). A steady, the people up front looked ‚Äúnormal‚Äù enough and didn‚Äôt have that gym rat mentality. They definitely tried to up sell services, but were not pushy. Funniest thing was it took some time to figure out the Bike and weight machines. Pedal power for the bike to start the time (who knew) and different settings along with traditional pins for the weight machines. Oh how things have changed.

I definitely prefer being outdoors, biking, golfing or swimming but this is a good alternative for the winter months. Pretty good deal for two years at Costco too.<//Review>

<Rate>4<//Rate><review>Perfect place, perfect ambience! I visited this library a few months back and I was very much impressed with its location, lighting, pleasing atmosphere, available topics and arrangement of books, ease of location and access, nice seating, all make it a beautiful library that you feel you should visit often. The registration is very simple and immediate that you can start borrowing number of books and videos at once. You have books on all topics, say, Fiction, non- Fiction, technical, political, educational and so on. You can browse through monitors and make a choice on author or title. This is a free library.
I was surprised to see that there are books on Indian languages like Tamil too.
You have video section too serving movie buffs and others. Number of DVDs and Blu-ray  movies, starting from age old 60's to modern day wait for you to grab. They have latest too. I was delightd to see some old movies too in their collection. There are interesting topics on non-fiction too.
You have facilities for copying, reading leisurely, self ticketing to borrow etc. Rest rooms are good. Parking is very nearby.
The staff are friendly and helpful. You can extend the books on line if required.
This library has kid section too, which is a plus point. While the reading habits are slowly coming down, the introduction of books to children  at an early age is a must to search and gain knowledge instead of digital hunting, Copy-Paste attitude.
Another thing I should mention is the beautiful architecture of the building. Lovely and invites you to visit.
The authorities should be appreciated for all their efforts in maintaining this treasure house of books in excellent condition. Hats off to them!
A place you must visit .<//review><pictures>None< /pictures><Resp>None< /Resp><Gmap_id>0x808fc975895448cd:0x485e82470495f7e1< /Gmap_id></record></dataset><record>

Available facilities are so high that you will overwhelm with those. One day I was asking for librarians that how much books I can take at a time. I was shocked with answer and ask her again. I was not able to believe on my ears. She said 60.

<Response>None<//Response><Rating>3</Rating><userid>108375423594010502389< /userid><date>1484374383297< /date><pics>None<//pics><Review>Please increase hours at a few libraries, have a few 24 hr libraries or open very early rather than having so many fancy smhancy branches. Public libraries are the last place where people with no/few resources can gain the knowledge and skills to compete with people with much higher resources. Investment in public libraries have way more multiplier effects and lead to social mobility than investment in roads and fancy buildings. This is especially true in Silicon Valley where the high cost of living keeps people with low resources out. Incumbents will always try to increase the barrier to entry and to create monopolies, and it will protect their interests in the short term. However in the long term, these incumbents who try to build barriers to entry will drive the innovators away to Texas or Boston with much lower cost of living, leading to lower innovation and SV will die a slow death. You as public libraries have this opportunity to lower the barrier to entry and drive innovation and growth in SV more than any other entity, if you chose to take on this role.</Review></record>

Small but exciting! Lots of different wildlife exhibits with an assortment of interesting animals to learn about. Two separate kids' play areas (a pretend "vet" spot and a place for smaller kids with blocks and books). Clean bathrooms, helpful and friendly staff, overall a great place to take small children. Not very crowded early on the weekend. <rating>4< /rating>< Text>
The place is small but pack with different things. It kept my 11 year old very engaged but my 8 and 5 year old did not stay entertained as long. The place has a natural history area with stuffed animals, preserved bird and insects, mineral exhibit, and more.l downstairs. Upstairs they have many exhibits with animals to see like birds, porcupines, snakes, roadrunner, rats, and more. While we were there they had a person showing off a gopher snake that the kids could touch. They have shows but do to the times it did not work into our schedule. We were able to get free passes for two of us through Discovery Go with my library card. There is a nice park with playground and grass area outside.< /Text>

<UserId.>102193855362654195370</UserId.><Name>Allyse Tanovitz</Name>< Time>
1534956592512</Time>
<rating>4</rating>< Text>
Awesome place to go to but it is pretty pricey for what you get. However I would recommend every local person attend, it is amazing the work they do for the animals. There is a behind the scenes vet room, you can see many birds of prey up close. There are all sorts of critters in nice cages, play room, animal make believe stuff, movie documentaries, experts, opportunities to touch certain animals. They had a porcupine the last time we went in August 2018. I love the owls, they're my favorite! There's also an eagle, pretty awesome! All the animals are rescued, many are returned back to the wild, but the ones who can't survive are kept here or sent to a zoo.
There is also a really nice park attached to it called Larkey Park. There are bathrooms inside the facility, they are nice, and drinking water. Outside there are also bathrooms as you walk down the path toward the park. There is also a walking trail that heads out from the park, too. And there is an amazing swimming pool and splash area. So if you want to come for the day you can bring a whole picnic thing, water gear, and some cash and you'll have an amazing fun day!<//Text>

<UserId.>104055297667842987283< /UserId.><gmapID>0x8085617b18ee1597:0x79fc6e28e8d229dc< /gmapID><resp>None<//resp><review>Nice place for a fun visit. They have an outdoor "raptor recess" area where they take the raptors out for daily exercise. They also have an indoor exhibit where the birds of prey stay, and also other animals like a porcupine, opossum, rabbit, etc. They have a theater room with one way glass so you can watch a part of their animal hospital, and other daily activities. I would definitely check the website or call ahead to see what they have when, so you can go when they have the activities you want to see. This is also home to the oldest living turkey vulture known in captivity. Great place to take the kids, and lots of fun/cool stuff in the gift shop.< /review>< Rate>

< text>
This is a great place to see rehabilitated animals that would not necessarily survive on their own in the wild. We saw owls, hawks, an entire active bee hive, snakes, rabbits, guinea pigs, a porcupine, and an eagle.

Plus if you‚Äôre lucky enough to be part of a tour of the hospital side, you can also see animals that are being nursed back to health for release back into the wild.< /text>

<Date>1567615153161< /Date>< Rating>

< text>
Where else, other than Hogwarts, can you see so many gorgeous owls? The owls are my favorite but there are also other raptors including a bald eagle, snakes, possums and more, all native California creatures that have been rescued due to injury or other issues. It's relatively small, but very accessible for the younger set. The interactive exhibits were especially popular with the 3-10 year olds. The 3 and 5 year olds with me really enjoyed the veterinary dress up area where they engaged in an extended imaginative play session. They also have really interesting presentations throughout the day. While we were there we watched volunteers and a vet do the health intake exam on a family of baby squirrels whose nest had fallen from a tree. It's attached to a nice park with a playground and plenty of room for picnicking. If you find a wild bird or creature in distress this is the place to take them!</text>

< Name>

< date>
1492582298474< /date>
< rate>
5</rate>
< Text>
Cool education place to bring babies and young children, especially when it's cold and rainy. There is always a "talk" by one of the volunteer wildlife ambassadors educating the kids about the local wildlife and the differences between wildlife and pets.  Beware: The volunteers do feed the birds dead mice and other things while speaking.

In the Exhibit hall is on one floor and is small. You can easily see everything in one hour. but can stay longer for each "talk" (one per 30 minutes to an hour). There is a bird area that there are live birds and owls sitting above the glass enclosed bird habitats, which you think are stuffed because the birds don't move at all.

Lots of interactive exhibits for kids of all ages to engage and learn from. The active bee hive is very cool by the window - the bees come in and out from outside and go into the clear "hive" to made honey.

There are live snakes, bunny, guinea pig, mice, rat, possum and a tarantula to look at. Lindsay is also an active wildlife rehabilitation hospital for the East Bay and offers wildlife education programs and camps starting at the age of 2 through teens throughout the year at very reasonable rates.

Another great value, become a annual Lindsay member and you can also get in free or get a 50% discount to visit six Bay Area science attractions, including Oakland Zoo, and more than 300 across the United States.

Diaper changing table in the women's restroom. Tiny-sized elevator to get up to the Exhibit Hall. In a residential neighborhood, Lindsay has access to additional free parking across the street at the church's parking lot.<//Text>

< Rating>
5</Rating>
<text>Excellent place to bring kids for a "field trip". Even fun for adults. I had the opportunity to be a volunteer a few years ago, and even though I was doing laundry and food dishes and cage cleaning, it was fun. The best part was feeding the animals. I got to feed a baby raccoon and we fed little birds 3 times a shift. This place is a hidden gem. If you find an injured bird or animal, they must be native to California. If not, they have to euthanize them. Call them if you do find an injured and they will usually tell you at that time whether they can treat or not.< /text>< pictures>

< rating>
4</rating>
< Text>
It's a working hospital first, a museum second. Not knowing that, it may seem uptight, but that's what a proper hospital should be. Professional medical establishments usually equate to uptight, so do not expect Disney world :)

One negative thing:

I hated to see the owls and falcons tethered to the top of shelves (they are not moved after hours).

It looked like opossum and there porcupine were a little cage crazy, but I'm not an expert on these matters. But man are some of those cages tiny.

This is a private hospital, and very well funded. But that shouldn't detract from giving the unreleasable indoor animals a little more space.< /Text>

<Date>1488053180827< /Date>< Review>
One of my favorite places to visit . they help domestic animals and birds that was hurt. Its one of the best places for kids to learn and be exposed to wild life. Animals are taken good care of all resques I believe . people find them and bring them to the museum they have great staff. This is a place where you and your kids can touch a snake , pat a bunny see bees and a queen bee , look at owls , turtle , snakes. There us a room for the little ones to play . will chair accessible . You can watch how they do daily routine check ups of patients with a live explanation of their actions .
Great , great , great place please do visit ! Parking structures available , playground right on a side of the museum. Sprouts close by so you can get your groceries on the way home. Fwy close by as well as close by downtown pleasanthill and walnut creek .< /Review>

<Name>Amy Palmer< /Name>< pictures>
None<//pictures>
<Date>1421048956287< /Date>< Text>
5/22/13

NOT THE BEST PLACE FOR PEOPLE WITH ORNITHOPHOBIA

There are some seriously cool birds inside the Lindsay Museum, and although some are in cages with glass windows, many sit tethered on top. Like the Giant Bald Eagle. And the Great Owl. It's pretty cool, though, you begin to feel a little bad for the birds. How long could I possibly sit in one spot comfortably? Hmm.

I came here a lot as a child (we lived on Larkey Lane so the park was my spot). It was in a different building then, which still sits next door and looks like it's not being used for anything. Not sure if they have storage or equipment in here but it's definitely not open to the public. I wish It were! Lots of good memories in the big building.

Lindsay has demos and hands-on interaction that your kids will enjoy. The downstairs is a large, open room and has art for sale on the wall and items like puzzles for kids to put together. It's pretty open and always surprises me that they don't do more with the space. It's fun to walk around the place from time to time but I'm sure it's a much great joy to experience this with a child. I think my favorite part of the Museum was the live bee hive with clear walls that has a tube connecting it to the outside world. We watched bees loaded with pollen come and make deliveries to their Queen. She's marked and pretty easy to find inside the hive. Really neat!

If you find a wild animal with an injury, bring it here and they'll patch it up. But if they determine the animal is too friendly, like their fox, they'll cage it up too and put it on display...which kind of sucks for Mr. Friendly Fox.< /Text>
